        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1106481217?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anmiryam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anmiryam" href="/user/show/2490546-anmiryam">Anmiryam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490546-anmiryam?shelf=print-arc">print-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490546-anmiryam?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490546-anmiryam?shelf=popular-fiction-2015">popular-fiction-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490546-anmiryam?shelf=malewriters-2015">malewriters-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490546-anmiryam?shelf=moc-2015">moc-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106481217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2723065382273383765">The sparkle and gleeful playfulness of the first book has congealed into an overlong, over plotted and orgiastic mess of consumer idiocy in this second installment in the saga of Rachel Chu and Nick Young, Astrid Leong and others.<br/><br/>Kwan should have stuck to the central Singaporean setting and his central characters rather than introducing a whole raft of new figures (too puppet-like to call characters) and multiplying his storylines. The saddest thing is that in nearly 400 pages he still doesn't r</span>
  <span id="freeText2723065382273383765" style="display:none">The sparkle and gleeful playfulness of the first book has congealed into an overlong, over plotted and orgiastic mess of consumer idiocy in this second installment in the saga of Rachel Chu and Nick Young, Astrid Leong and others.<br /><br />Kwan should have stuck to the central Singaporean setting and his central characters rather than introducing a whole raft of new figures (too puppet-like to call characters) and multiplying his storylines. The saddest thing is that in nearly 400 pages he still doesn't resolve the central question: will Nick's grandmother forgive his choice of bride and reinstate him as heir? I think we will be forced to plow through an additional volume to learn the answer to these and other not-so-compelling bits of information.<br /><br />Really, I hate it when a series falls this far, this fast. Still, I read it open-mouthed at the proliferation of brand names I've never actually heard of before and the over-the-top reportage of egregious consumption. Best on an airplane or on a beach.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2723065382273383765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1359404214" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1359404214" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23315273-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546293743p2/23315273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1359404214?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/23315273-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=humor-satire">humor-satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=china-hongkong-nepal-taiwan">china-hongkong-nepal-taiwan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1359404214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16899994374101063915">China Rich Girlfriend is a blast. <br/><br/>*Backing up a step, I started with CRG. I hadn't read Crazy Rich Asians and CRG stood on its own, e.g., I wasn't lacking any necessary background material and also didn't suffer through 20 pages of material designed to catch-up a new reader. So . . . don't feel as though you can't pick up this novel because it's the second in a series. <br/><br/>I enjoyed the structure of having a variety of plotlines and characters. I liked some more than others. Rachel and Astrid are de</span>
  <span id="freeText16899994374101063915" style="display:none">China Rich Girlfriend is a blast. <br /><br />*Backing up a step, I started with CRG. I hadn't read Crazy Rich Asians and CRG stood on its own, e.g., I wasn't lacking any necessary background material and also didn't suffer through 20 pages of material designed to catch-up a new reader. So . . . don't feel as though you can't pick up this novel because it's the second in a series. <br /><br />I enjoyed the structure of having a variety of plotlines and characters. I liked some more than others. Rachel and Astrid are delightful. Several others are less than delightful, but Kwan moved from one set to another sufficiently quickly that the less-than-delightful characters didn't cause me to want to exit the book. Loved, loved, loved the "educational" footnotes. I was oblivious to the social dynamics in Singapore and mainland Chinese who've become financially successful in the last couple of decades. I learned more from this book, while having fun, than I have from most of the historical novels I convince myself are educational. Ha!<br /><br />This novel reminded me of Who's Afraid of Bernadette?, a book club favorite of a couple of years ago that skewered the Seattle tech and social culture. I didn't get what my friends saw in that novel and found it shallow and I couldn't identify with any of the characters. I'm sure that some readers might have the same reaction to China Rich Girlfriend, which applies a similar jaundiced observant eye to young Asian globetrotters and their families. For me, though Kwan has just the right touch of comedy and depth to make this an enjoyable read, and I'm looking forward to his next novel, as well as his first.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16899994374101063915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AVPG2hJTJNLJmfVa3D1kWMnXiU7EocC0NafFWClBxNLuhn8fqBJUbU4RvOkq8oDFAqx4ViA+gUSkJi1AbYDLIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7nv8cbLcaK7cP4fVnwIkCBrpJaCrWzf5XItqOeMN5mwBrkW0CJ0YEVu3zmZpzcCV0ZLUuE/EdgnNCoIhp8zpng==')})
  }

But after growing up together in a small, southern black community and running away at age sixteen, it\'s not just the shape of their daily lives that is different as adults, it\'s everything: their families, their communities, their racial identities. Many years later, one sister lives with her black daughter in the same southern town she once tried to escape. The other secretly passes for white, and her white husband knows nothing of her past. Still, even separated by so many miles and just as many lies, the fates of the twins remain intertwined. What will happen to the next generation, when their own daughters\' storylines intersect?\n\nWeaving together multiple strands and generations of this family, from the Deep South to California, from the 1950s to the 1990s, Brit Bennett produces a story that is at once a riveting, emotional family story and a brilliant exploration of the American history of passing. Looking well beyond issues of race, The Vanishing Half considers the lasting influence of the past as it shapes a person\'s decisions, desires, and expectations, and explores some of the multiple <span id="freeTextContainer6967147614435428340">KEVIN KWAN is the author of Crazy Rich Asians, the international bestselling novel that has been translated into more than 30 languages. Its sequel, China Rich Girlfriend, was released in 2015, and Rich People Problems, the final book in the trilogy, followed in 2017.   <span id="freeText6967147614435428340" style="display:none">KEVIN KWAN is the author of Crazy Rich Asians, the international bestselling novel that has been translated into more than 30 languages. Its sequel, China Rich Girlfriend, was released in 2015, and Rich People Problems, the final book in the trilogy, followed in 2017. For several weeks in 2018, the Crazy Rich Asians trilogy commanded the top three positions of the New York Times bestseller list - an almost unprecedented single-author trifecta, and the film adaptation of Crazy Rich Asians became Hollywood's highest grossing romantic comedy in over a decade. In 2018, Kevin was named by Time Magazine as one of the 100 Most Influential People in the World.<br /><br />Please visit Kevin at:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.kevinkwanbooks.com">www.kevinkwanbooks.com</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/KevinKwanBooks">https://www.facebook.com/KevinKwanBooks</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://instagram.com/kevinkwanbooks/">https://instagram.com/kevinkwanbooks/</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/kevinkwanbooks">https://twitter.com/kevinkwanbooks</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.pinterest.com/kevinkwanbooks/">https://www.pinterest.com/kevinkwanbo...</a><br /><br /></span>

What she doesn\'t know is that Nick\'s family home happens to look like a palace, that she\'ll ride in more private planes than cars, and that with one of Asia\'s most eligible bachelors on her arm, Rachel might as well have a target on her back.\n\nInitiated into a world of dynastic splendor beyond imagination, Rachel meets Astrid, the It Girl of Singapore society; Eddie, whose family practically lives in the pages of the Hong Kong socialite magazines; and Eleanor, Nick\'s formidable mother, a woman who has very strong feelings about who her son should--and should not--marry. Uproarious, addictive, and filled with jaw-dropping opulence, Crazy Rich Asians is an insider\'s look at the Asian JetSet; a perfect depiction of the clash between old money and new money; between Overseas Chinese and Mainland Chinese; and a fabulous novel about what it means to be young, in love, and gloriously, crazily rich.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16845325528024312987\" href=\"#\"
